The `ObligationForest` is a utility data structure used in trait\n     2→//! matching to track the set of outstanding obligations (those not yet\n     3→//! resolved to success or error). It also tracks the \"backtrace\" of each\n     4→//! pending obligation (why we are trying to figure this out in the first\n     5→//! place).\n     6→//!\n     7→//! ### External view\n     8→//!\n     9→//! `ObligationForest` supports two main public operations (there are a\n    10→//! few others not discussed here):\n    11→//!\n    12→//! 1. Add a new root obligations (`register_obligation`).\n    13→//! 2. Process the pending obligations (`process_obligations`).\n    14→//!\n    15→//! When a new obligation `N` is added, it becomes the root of an\n    16→//! obligation tree. This tree can also carry some per-tree state `T`,\n    17→//! which is given at the same time. This tree is a singleton to start, so\n    18→//! `N` is both the root and the only leaf. Each time the\n    19→//! `process_obligations` method is called, it will invoke its callback\n    20→//! with every pending obligation (so that will include `N`, the first\n    21→//! time). The callback also receives a (mutable) reference to the\n    22→//! per-tree state `T`. The callback should process the obligation `O`\n    23→//! that it is given and return a `ProcessResult`:\n    24→//!\n    25→//! - `Unchanged` -> ambiguous result. Obligation was neither a success\n    26→//!   nor a failure. It is assumed that further attempts to process the\n    27→//!   obligation will yield the same result unless something in the\n    28→//!   surrounding environment changes.\n    29→//! - `Changed(C)` - the obligation was *shallowly successful*. The\n    30→//!   vector `C` is a list of subobligations. The meaning of this is that\n    31→//!   `O` was successful on the assumption that all the obligations in `C`\n    32→//!   are also successful. Therefore, `O` is only considered a \"true\"\n    33→//!   success if `C` is empty. Otherwise, `O` is put into a suspended\n    34→//!   state and the obligations in `C` become the new pending\n    35→//!   obligations. They will be processed the next time you call\n    36→//!   `process_obligations`.\n    37→//! - `Error(E)` -> obligation failed with error `E`. We will collect this\n    38→//!   error and return it from `process_obligations`, along with the\n    39→//!   \"backtrace\" of obligations (that is, the list of obligations up to\n    40→//!   and including the root of the failed obligation). No further\n    41→//!   obligations from that same tree will be processed, since the tree is\n    42→//!   now considered to be in error.\n    43→//!\n    44→//! When the call to `process_obligations` completes, you get back an `Outcome`,\n    45→//! which includes two bits of information:\n    46→//!\n    47→//! - `completed`: a list of obligations where processing was fully\n    48→//!   completed without error (meaning that all transitive subobligations\n    49→//!   have also been completed). The `ObligationForest` is a utility data structure used in trait\n//! matching to track the set of outstanding obligations (those not yet\n//! resolved to success or error). It also tracks the \"backtrace\" of each\n//! pending obligation (why we are trying to figure this out in the first\n//! place).\n//!\n//! ### External view\n//!\n//! `ObligationForest` supports two main public operations (there are a\n//! few others not discussed here):\n//!\n//! 1. Add a new root obligations (`register_obligation`).\n//! 2. Process the pending obligations (`process_obligations`).\n//!\n//! When a new obligation `N` is added, it becomes the root of an\n//! obligation tree. This tree can also carry some per-tree state `T`,\n//! which is given at the same time. This tree is a singleton to start, so\n//! `N` is both the root and the only leaf. Each time the\n//! `process_obligations` method is called, it will invoke its callback\n//! with every pending obligation (so that will include `N`, the first\n//! time). The callback also receives a (mutable) reference to the\n//! per-tree state `T`. The callback should process the obligation `O`\n//! that it is given and return a `ProcessResult`:\n//!\n//! - `Unchanged` -> ambiguous result. Obligation was neither a success\n//!   nor a failure. It is assumed that further attempts to process the\n//!   obligation will yield the same result unless something in the\n//!   surrounding environment changes.\n//! - `Changed(C)` - the obligation was *shallowly successful*. The\n//!   vector `C` is a list of subobligations. The meaning of this is that\n//!   `O` was successful on the assumption that all the obligations in `C`\n//!   are also successful. Therefore, `O` is only considered a \"true\"\n//!   success if `C` is empty. Otherwise, `O` is put into a suspended\n//!   state and the obligations in `C` become the new pending\n//!   obligations. They will be processed the next time you call\n//!   `process_obligations`.\n//! - `Error(E)` -> obligation failed with error `E`. We will collect this\n//!   error and return it from `process_obligations`, along with the\n//!   \"backtrace\" of obligations (that is, the list of obligations up to\n//!   and including the root of the failed obligation). No further\n//!   obligations from that same tree will be processed, since the tree is\n//!   now considered to be in error.\n//!\n//! When the call to `process_obligations` completes, you get back an `Outcome`,\n//! which includes two bits of information:\n//!\n//! - `completed`: a list of obligations where processing was fully\n//!   completed without error (meaning that all transitive subobligations\n//!   have also been completed). So, for example, if the callback from\n//!   `process_obligations` returns `Changed(C)` for some obligation `O`,\n//!   then `O` will be considered completed right away if `C` is the\n//!   empty vector. Otherwise it will only be considered completed once\n//!   all the obligations in `C` have been found completed.\n//! - `errors`: a list of errors that occurred and associated backtraces\n//!   at the time of error, which can be used to give context to the user.\n//!\n//! Upon completion, none of the existing obligations were *shallowly\n//! successful* (that is, no callback returned `Changed(_)`). This implies that\n//! all obligations were either errors or returned an ambiguous result.\n//!\n//! ### Implementation details\n//!\n//! For the most part, comments specific to the implementation are in the\n//! code. This file only contains a very high-level overview. Basically,\n//! the forest is stored in a vector. Each element of the vector is a node\n//! in some tree. Each node in the vector has the index of its dependents,\n//! including the first dependent which is known as the parent. It also\n//! has a current state, described by `NodeState`. After each processing\n//! step, we compress the vector to remove completed and error nodes, which\n//! aren't needed anymore.\n\nuse std::cell::Cell;\nuse std::collections::hash_map::Entry;\nuse std::fmt::Debug;\nuse std::hash;\nuse std::marker::PhantomData;\n\nuse thin_vec::ThinVec;\nuse tracing::debug;\n\nuse crate::fx::{FxHashMap, FxHashSet};\n\nmod graphviz;\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests;\n\npub trait ForestObligation: Clone + Debug {\n    type CacheKey: Clone + hash::Hash + Eq + Debug;\n\n    /// Converts this `ForestObligation` suitable for use as a cache key.\n    /// If two distinct `ForestObligations`s return the same cache key,\n    /// then it must be sound to use the result of processing one obligation\n    /// (e.g. success for error) for the other obligation\n    fn as_cache_key(&self) -> Self::CacheKey;\n}\n\npub trait ObligationProcessor {\n    type Obligation: ForestObligation;\n    type Error: Debug;","numLines":100,"startLine":1,"totalLines":743}}}

Basically, a freshly incremented counter.\n    dfn: usize,\n}\n\nstruct SelectionCandidateSet<'tcx> {\n    /// A list of candidates that definitely apply to the current\n    /// obligation (meaning: types unify).\n    vec: Vec<SelectionCandidate<'tcx>>,\n\n    /// If `true`, then there were candidates that might or might\n    /// not have applied, but we couldn't tell. See\n    /// the documentation of [`Self::intercrate_ambiguity_causes`] for more.\n    pub fn enable_tracking_intercrate_ambiguity_causes(&mut self) {\n        assert_matches!(self.infcx.typing_mode(), TypingMode::Coherence);\n        assert!(self.intercrate_ambiguity_causes.is_none());\n        self.intercrate_ambiguity_causes = Some(FxIndexSet::default());\n        debug!(\"selcx: enable_tracking_intercrate_ambiguity_causes\");\n    }\n\n    /// Gets the intercrate ambiguity causes collected since tracking\n    /// was enabled and disables tracking at the same time. For example, it will identify which impl or\n    // parameter bound is to be used. The process can be inconclusive\n    // if the self type in the obligation is not fully inferred. Selection\n    // can result in an error in one of two ways:\n    //\n    // 1. If no applicable impl or parameter bound can be found.\n    // 2. self.select_from_obligation(obligation) {\n            Err(SelectionError::Overflow(OverflowError::Canonical)) => {\n                // In standard mode, overflow must have been caught and reported\n                // earlier.\n                assert!(self.query_mode == TraitQueryMode::Canonical);\n                return Err(SelectionError::Overflow(OverflowError::Canonical));\n            }\n Propagate overflow if it occurs.\n        let candidates = candidates\n            .into_iter()\n            .map(|c| match self.evaluate_candidate(stack, &c) {\n                Ok(eval) if eval.may_apply() => {\n                    Ok(Some(EvaluatedCandidate { candidate: c, evaluation: eval }))\n                }\n                Ok(_) => Ok(None),\n                Err(OverflowError::Canonical) => {\n                    Err(SelectionError::Overflow(OverflowError::Canonical))\n                }\n                Err(OverflowError::Error(e)) => {\n                    Err(SelectionError::Overflow(OverflowError::Error(e)))\n                }\n            })\n            .flat_map(Result::transpose)\n            .collect::<Result<Vec<_>, _>>()?;\n\n        debug!(?stack, ?candidates, \"{} potentially applicable candidates\", candidates.len());\n        // If there are *NO* candidates, then there are no impls --\n        // that we know of, anyway. Note that in the case where there\n        // are unbound type variables within the obligation, it might\n        // be the case that you could still satisfy the obligation\n        // from another crate by instantiating the type variables with\n        // a type from another crate that does have an impl. This case\n        // is checked for in `evaluate_stack` (and hence users\n        // who might care about this case, like coherence, should use\n        // that function).\n        if candidates.is_empty() {\n            // If there's an error type, 'downgrade' our result from\n            // `Err(Unimplemented)` to `Ok(None)`. This helps us avoid\n            // emitting additional spurious errors, since we're guaranteed\n            // to have emitted at least one.\n            if stack.obligation.predicate.references_error() {\n                debug!(?stack.obligation.predicate, \"found error type in predicate, treating as ambiguous\");\n                Ok(None)\n            } else {\n                Err(SelectionError::Unimplemented)\n            }\n        } else {\n            let has_non_region_infer = stack.obligation.predicate.has_non_region_infer();\n            let candidate_preference_mode =\n                CandidatePreferenceMode::compute(self.tcx(), stack.obligation.predicate.def_id());\n            if let Some(candidate) =\n                self.winnow_candidates(has_non_region_infer, candidate_preference_mode, candidates)\n            {\n                self.filter_reservation_impls(candidate)\n            } else {\n                Ok(None)\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    ///////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////\n    // EVALUATION\n    //\n    // Tests whether an obligation can be selected or whether an impl\n    // can be applied to particular types. It skips the \"confirmation\"\n    // step and hence completely ignores output type parameters.\n    //\n    // The result is \"true\" if the obligation *may* hold and \"false\" if\n    // we can be sure it does not.","numLines":200,"startLine":300,"totalLines":3207}}}

Rust trait obligation system works through a carefully orchestrated chain of components that manages trait solving from registration through error reporting.\\n\\n**Core Data Structure: ObligationForest**\\nThe foundation is `ObligationForest` in `compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs`. It manages a forest of obligation nodes, supporting two main operations: adding root obligations and processing pending obligations. It implements a tree structure where each node can spawn child obligations and tracks completion or error states.\\n\\n**Fulfillment Context and Processing**\\nThe `FulfillmentContext` (in `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs`) is the main entry point for trait solving. It wraps an `ObligationForest` of `PendingPredicateObligation` nodes and drives the solving process. When `select()` is called, it creates a `FulfillProcessor` that implements the `ObligationProcessor` trait.\\n\\n**The FulfillProcessor Chain**\\n`FulfillProcessor::process_obligation()` is the key method that processes each pending obligation. For trait obligations, it routes to `process_trait_obligation()`, which calls `SelectionContext::poly_select()` to attempt trait selection. The processor handles different predicate kinds (trait, projection, well-formedness, subtyping, etc.) and converts selection results into `ProcessResult` values: `Changed` (obligation satisfied with subobligations), `Unchanged` (ambiguous), or `Error`.\\n\\n**Selection Pipeline: Candidate Assembly and Matching**\\nThe `SelectionContext` (in `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs`) is the core selection engine. It implements the key methods:\\n- `poly_select()`: Entry point for selecting a polymorphic trait obligation\\n- `candidate_from_obligation()`: Attempts to find a candidate with caching\\n- `candidate_from_obligation_no_cache()`: Core logic that assembles and filters candidates\\n\\nCandidate assembly is handled in `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/candidate_assembly.rs` with `assemble_candidates()`. This method collects all applicable candidates from:\\n- Trait aliases (`assemble_candidates_for_trait_alias`)\\n- Impl blocks (`assemble_candidates_from_impls`)\\n- Caller bounds (`assemble_candidates_from_caller_bounds`)\\n- Builtin candidates for special traits (Sized, Clone, etc.)\\n\\n**Impl Matching**\\nImplementation matching uses `MatchAgainstFreshVars` in `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/_match.rs`. This implements the `TypeRelation` trait to check if a trait reference structurally matches a freshened impl signature. The matcher allows unbound type variables in the impl but ensures concrete types in the obligation match exactly.\\n\\n**Candidate Confirmation**\\nOnce a candidate is selected, `SelectionContext::confirm_candidate()` in `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs` confirms it and generates obligations. For impl candidates, this calls `confirm_impl_candidate()` which unifies output types and collects nested obligations from the impl. Different candidate types (ParamCandidate, ImplCandidate, BuiltinCandidate, ProjectionCandidate, ClosureCandidate, etc.) are confirmed differently.\\n\\n**Specialization**\\nWhen multiple impls apply, specialization rules in `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/specialize/mod.rs` determine precedence. The specialization graph tracks impl relationships to ensure only the most specific impl is selected.\\n\\n**Error Reporting**\\nUnsatisfied trait bounds are reported by `FulfillmentErrorCode` and handled in `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/fulfillment_errors.rs` and `mod.rs`. The error reporting system generates detailed diagnostics including:\\n- What trait failed to be satisfied\\n- Why it failed (unimplemented, unsatisfied bounds, ambiguity)\\n- Suggestions for fixes (adding bounds, using different types)\\n- On-unimplemented attribute messages\\n\\n**The Obligation Chain Execution**\\nWhen a trait obligation is registered with `FulfillmentContext`, it enters the ObligationForest as a root node. Each `process_obligations()` iteration applies `FulfillProcessor` to pending nodes. A trait obligation flows through: initial registration → trait selection attempt → candidate assembly → impl matching → confirmation with nested obligations → eventual completion or error. The processor handles different predicate kinds (trait, projection, well-formedness, subtyping, etc.) and converts selection results into `ProcessResult` values: `Changed` (obligation satisfied with subobligations), `Unchanged` (ambiguous), or `Error`.\\n\\n**Selection Pipeline: Candidate Assembly and Matching**\\nThe `SelectionContext` (in `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs`) is the core selection engine. It implements the key methods:\\n- `poly_select()`: Entry point for selecting a polymorphic trait obligation\\n- `candidate_from_obligation()`: Attempts to find a candidate with caching\\n- `candidate_from_obligation_no_cache()`: Core logic that assembles and filters candidates\\n\\nCandidate assembly is handled in `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/candidate_assembly.rs` with `assemble_candidates()`. This method collects all applicable candidates from:\\n- Trait aliases (`assemble_candidates_for_trait_alias`)\\n- Impl blocks (`assemble_candidates_from_impls`)\\n- Caller bounds (`assemble_candidates_from_caller_bounds`)\\n- Builtin candidates for special traits (Sized, Clone, etc.)\\n\\n**Impl Matching**\\nImplementation matching uses `MatchAgainstFreshVars` in `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/_match.rs`. This implements the `TypeRelation` trait to check if a trait reference structurally matches a freshened impl signature. The matcher allows unbound type variables in the impl but ensures concrete types in the obligation match exactly.\\n\\n**Candidate Confirmation**\\nOnce a candidate is selected, `SelectionContext::confirm_candidate()` in `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs` confirms it and generates obligations. For impl candidates, this calls `confirm_impl_candidate()` which unifies output types and collects nested obligations from the impl. Different candidate types (ParamCandidate, ImplCandidate, BuiltinCandidate, ProjectionCandidate, ClosureCandidate, etc.) are confirmed differently.\\n\\n**Specialization**\\nWhen multiple impls apply, specialization rules in `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/specialize/mod.rs` determine precedence. The specialization graph tracks impl relationships to ensure only the most specific impl is selected.\\n\\n**Error Reporting**\\nUnsatisfied trait bounds are reported by `FulfillmentErrorCode` and handled in `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/fulfillment_errors.rs` and `mod.rs`. The error reporting system generates detailed diagnostics including:\\n- What trait failed to be satisfied\\n- Why it failed (unimplemented, unsatisfied bounds, ambiguity)\\n- Suggestions for fixes (adding bounds, using different types)\\n- On-unimplemented attribute messages\\n\\n**The Obligation Chain Execution**\\nWhen a trait obligation is registered with `FulfillmentContext`, it enters the ObligationForest as a root node. Each `process_obligations()` iteration applies `FulfillProcessor` to pending nodes. A trait obligation flows through: initial registration → trait selection attempt → candidate assembly → impl matching → confirmation with nested obligations → eventual completion or error. Failed obligations generate error entries with their full obligation stack for diagnostic context.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

works through a carefully orchestrated chain of components that manages trait solving from registration through error reporting.\\n\\n**Core Data Structure: ObligationForest**\\nThe foundation is `ObligationForest` in `compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs`. It manages a forest of obligation nodes, supporting two main operations: adding root obligations and processing pending obligations. It implements a tree structure where each node can spawn child obligations and tracks completion or error states.\\n\\n**Fulfillment Context and Processing**\\nThe `FulfillmentContext` (in `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs`) is the main entry point for trait solving. When `select()` is called, it creates a `FulfillProcessor` that implements the `ObligationProcessor` trait.\\n\\n**The FulfillProcessor Chain**\\n`FulfillProcessor::process_obligation()` is the key method that processes each pending obligation. For trait obligations, it routes to `process_trait_obligation()`, which calls `SelectionContext::poly_select()` to attempt trait selection. The processor handles different predicate kinds (trait, projection, well-formedness, subtyping, etc.) and converts selection results into `ProcessResult` values: `Changed` (obligation satisfied with subobligations), `Unchanged` (ambiguous), or `Error`.\\n\\n**Selection Pipeline: Candidate Assembly and Matching**\\nThe `SelectionContext` (in `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs`) is the core selection engine. The matcher allows unbound type variables in the impl but ensures concrete types in the obligation match exactly.\\n\\n**Candidate Confirmation**\\nOnce a candidate is selected, `SelectionContext::confirm_candidate()` in `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs` confirms it and generates obligations. The specialization graph tracks impl relationships to ensure only the most specific impl is selected.\\n\\n**Error Reporting**\\nUnsatisfied trait bounds are reported by `FulfillmentErrorCode` and handled in `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/fulfillment_errors.rs` and `mod.rs`. Rust trait obligation system works through a carefully orchestrated chain of components that manages trait solving from registration through error reporting.\\n\\n**Core Data Structure: ObligationForest**\\nThe foundation is `ObligationForest` in `compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs`. It manages a forest of obligation nodes, supporting two main operations: adding root obligations and processing pending obligations. It implements a tree structure where each node can spawn child obligations and tracks completion or error states.\\n\\n**Fulfillment Context and Processing**\\nThe `FulfillmentContext` (in `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs`) is the main entry point for trait solving. It wraps an `ObligationForest` of `PendingPredicateObligation` nodes and drives the solving process. When `select()` is called, it creates a `FulfillProcessor` that implements the `ObligationProcessor` trait.\\n\\n**The FulfillProcessor Chain**\\n`FulfillProcessor::process_obligation()` is the key method that processes each pending obligation. For trait obligations, it routes to `process_trait_obligation()`, which calls `SelectionContext::poly_select()` to attempt trait selection. The processor handles different predicate kinds (trait, projection, well-formedness, subtyping, etc.) and converts selection results into `ProcessResult` values: `Changed` (obligation satisfied with subobligations), `Unchanged` (ambiguous), or `Error`.\\n\\n**Selection Pipeline: Candidate Assembly and Matching**\\nThe `SelectionContext` (in `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs`) is the core selection engine. It implements the key methods:\\n- `poly_select()`: Entry point for selecting a polymorphic trait obligation\\n- `candidate_from_obligation()`: Attempts to find a candidate with caching\\n- `candidate_from_obligation_no_cache()`: Core logic that assembles and filters candidates\\n\\nCandidate assembly is handled in `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/candidate_assembly.rs` with `assemble_candidates()`. This method collects all applicable candidates from:\\n- Trait aliases (`assemble_candidates_for_trait_alias`)\\n- Impl blocks (`assemble_candidates_from_impls`)\\n- Caller bounds (`assemble_candidates_from_caller_bounds`)\\n- Builtin candidates for special traits (Sized, Clone, etc.)\\n\\n**Impl Matching**\\nImplementation matching uses `MatchAgainstFreshVars` in `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/_match.rs`. This implements the `TypeRelation` trait to check if a trait reference structurally matches a freshened impl signature. The matcher allows unbound type variables in the impl but ensures concrete types in the obligation match exactly.\\n\\n**Candidate Confirmation**\\nOnce a candidate is selected, `SelectionContext::confirm_candidate()` in `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs` confirms it and generates obligations. For impl candidates, this calls `confirm_impl_candidate()` which unifies output types and collects nested obligations from the impl. Different candidate types (ParamCandidate, ImplCandidate, BuiltinCandidate, ProjectionCandidate, ClosureCandidate, etc.) are confirmed differently.\\n\\n**Specialization**\\nWhen multiple impls apply, specialization rules in `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/specialize/mod.rs` determine precedence. The specialization graph tracks impl relationships to ensure only the most specific impl is selected.\\n\\n**Error Reporting**\\nUnsatisfied trait bounds are reported by `FulfillmentErrorCode` and handled in `compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/fulfillment_errors.rs` and `mod.rs`. The error reporting system generates detailed diagnostics including:\\n- What trait failed to be satisfied\\n- Why it failed (unimplemented, unsatisfied bounds, ambiguity)\\n- Suggestions for fixes (adding bounds, using different types)\\n- On-unimplemented attribute messages\\n\\n**The Obligation Chain Execution**\\nWhen a trait obligation is registered with `FulfillmentContext`, it enters the ObligationForest as a root node. Each `process_obligations()` iteration applies `FulfillProcessor` to pending nodes. A trait obligation flows through: initial registration → trait selection attempt → candidate assembly → impl matching → confirmation with nested obligations → eventual completion or error. Failed obligations generate error entries with their full obligation stack for diagnostic context.\"\n}\n","numLines":186,"startLine":1,"totalLines":186}}}
